Module 01

    
What is ArgoCD?

    
The Kubernetes-native GitOps tool that makes Git your only deployment button — no more kubectl apply from CI pipelines

  


  

    
👶 ELI5

    
Imagine you have a security guard watching your Kubernetes cluster 24/7. He has a rulebook (your Git repo) that says exactly how the cluster should look. If someone sneaks in and manually changes a deployment — the guard notices the difference and puts it back. If you update the rulebook (push to Git) — the guard reads the new rules and updates the cluster automatically. That security guard is ArgoCD. Git is always boss.

  


  
  

    

      
😰 Before ArgoCD

      
Push-Based CD (The Problem)

      

# Jenkins/GitHub Actions pipeline:
kubectl apply -f deploy.yaml  # ← credentials in CI!
kubectl apply -f service.yaml
kubectl apply -f ingress.yaml

      
    
        
  • Cluster credentials stored in CI secrets
    • 
        
  • No drift detection — cluster can diverge from Git
    • 
        
  • Rollback = re-run old pipeline (if logs kept)
    • 
        
  • Who deployed what? Check CI logs... if they exist
    • 
        
  • Disaster recovery = run pipeline + pray
    • 
      

    

    

      
✅ With ArgoCD

      
Pull-Based GitOps (The Solution)

      

# Only command you need:
git push origin main
# ArgoCD detects → syncs → done ✓

      
    
        
  • Zero cluster credentials outside the cluster
    • 
        
  • Self-healing — drift reverted automatically
    • 
        
  • Rollback = git revert + push (90 seconds)
    • 
        
  • Full audit trail in Git — commit, author, PR, time
    • 
        
  • Disaster recovery = argocd sync (cluster rebuilt from Git)
    • 
      

    

  


  
  

    
🔄 DevOps Analogy

    
ArgoCD = Kubernetes' Desired State Enforcer

    

      

        📁
        
GitSingle source of truth — like Terraform state, but for live K8s objects

      

      

        🔄
        
ArgoCDThe reconciliation loop — constantly compares desired (Git) vs actual (cluster)

      

      

        ⚙️
        
Like systemdDefines what should run and restarts it if it drifts — but for your entire Kubernetes cluster

      

      

        🏗️
        
Like Terraformterraform plan = argocd app diff | terraform apply = argocd app sync

      

    

  


  
  
Key Concepts

  

    

      
📱

      
Application

      
CRD that defines source (Git path) + destination (cluster/namespace). One app per microservice.

    

    

      
🗂️

      
Project

      
RBAC boundary and namespace isolation. Team A can't deploy to Team B's namespace.

    

    

      
🔁

      
Sync

      
The act of applying Git state to the cluster. Can be manual (prod) or automated (dev/staging).

    

    

      
❤️

      
Health

      
Is the deployed resource actually working? Healthy/Degraded/Progressing — separate from Sync status.

    

    

      
📦

      
Repository

      
Git repo, Helm registry, or OCI registry that ArgoCD monitors for changes.

    

    

      
🌳

      
App-of-Apps

      
Parent Application that manages child ArgoCD Applications in Git. Scale to 100 services.

    

  


  
  

    
📊 Push CD vs GitOps

    

      

        
Traditional Push CDGitOps (ArgoCD)

        
          
Cluster credentialsIn CI (Jenkins / GitHub Actions secrets)Inside cluster only — never leaves

          
Drift detectionNone — cluster silently divergesAutomatic — alerts on OutOfSync

          
Audit trailCI logs (if not rotated)Full Git history: author, PR, timestamp

          
RollbackRe-run old pipeline, manuallygit revert + push → auto-synced

          
Disaster recoveryRe-run all pipelines + hopeargocd sync → cluster rebuilt from Git

          
Source of truthScattered: CI vars, scripts, manifestsGit — one place, one history

        
      

    

  








  

    
Module 02

    
GitOps — The Four Principles

    
Why GitOps exists and how it fundamentally changes your entire deployment model

  


  

    
👶 ELI5

    
GitOps = Ops done through Git. Instead of clicking buttons or running CLI commands to deploy, you commit to Git. An agent inside your cluster reads Git and makes reality match it. Always. Automatically. If reality drifts, the agent corrects it.

  


  
  


    

      
1

      

        
Declarative

        
Describe what you want, not how to get there. Write replicas: 3 in a YAML file — not kubectl scale --replicas=3 in a script. K8s manifests, Helm values, Kustomize overlays — all declarative by nature.

        

# Declarative (GitOps ✓)
spec:
  replicas: 3
  image: myapp:v2.0.0

# Imperative (not GitOps ✗)
kubectl scale deploy myapp --replicas=3
kubectl set image deploy/myapp app=myapp:v2.0.0

      

    


    

      
2

      

        
Versioned & Immutable

        
Git is the single source of truth. Every deployment change is a commit — immutable, timestamped, attributable. You can git log your deployments the same way you git log your code.

        

git log production/values.yaml
# a3f9c12  alice  bump image to v2.1.0  (2 hours ago)
# b7e4d80  bob    scale to 5 replicas    (yesterday)
# c9a1f35  alice  add readinessProbe     (3 days ago)

      

    


    

      
3

      

        
Pulled Automatically

        
The agent inside the cluster pulls changes from Git — not pushed from outside. The cluster reaches out to Git, not the other way around. No cluster credentials ever leave the cluster.

        

          

            
⬆️ PUSH (Old Way)

            

              
Developer

              
↓ git push

              
CI Pipeline

              
↓ kubectl apply
⚠️ cluster creds in CI!

              
K8s Cluster

            

          

          

            
⬇️ PULL (GitOps)

            

              
Developer

              
↓ git push

              
Git Repo

              
↓ ArgoCD polls
✅ creds inside cluster

              
K8s Cluster + ArgoCD

            

          

        

      

    


    

      
4

      

        
Continuously Reconciled

        
An automated agent runs forever — every 3 minutes by default — comparing desired state (Git) to actual state (cluster). Any drift is corrected. Self-healing is the default, not a feature you bolt on.

        

# Someone runs this manually at 3am:
kubectl scale deploy payments-api --replicas=1

# ArgoCD reconciliation loop (next cycle, ~3 min):
# Desired (Git): replicas: 3
# Actual (cluster): replicas: 1
# Action: kubectl apply → replicas restored to 3
# Alert: "OutOfSync detected and corrected"

      

    


  


  
  

    
🎬 Real Scenario

    
2:30 AM — Production down. 6 AM — your manager asks questions.

    

      

        
❌ Jenkins push pipeline:

        
Check CI logs — if not rotated. Hope the deploy step captured the image tag. The approver? Check Jira... maybe. The exact diff? Unavailable.

      

      

        
✅ GitOps with ArgoCD:

        
git log --since="yesterday" \
  production/values.yaml
# a3f9c12  alice@co.com
# "chore: bump payments-api to v2.1.0"
# PR #482, approved by: bob@co.com
# 2026-03-17 23:47:33 UTC

      

    

  


  
  

    
💡 GitOps vs DevOps

    
GitOps is not a replacement for DevOps — it's the deployment part of DevOps done declaratively through Git. CI still builds and tests your code. GitOps takes over at the "deploy to cluster" step. Think of it as: CI builds the artifact, GitOps delivers it.

  


        
        

          
📁 GitOps Repository Patterns — Where Do All the Files Go?

          
One of the first questions every new ArgoCD user has: "Where do I put my ArgoCD Application YAMLs and Helm charts?" There are two main patterns:

          

            

              
📦 Pattern 1: Monorepo

              
App code + K8s manifests in the same repo. Simple for small teams.

              
sre-autopilot/             ← one repo
├── app/                   ← FastAPI code
│   ├── main.py
│   └── Dockerfile
├── helm/                  ← Helm chart
│   ├── Chart.yaml
│   ├── values.yaml
│   └── templates/
└── argocd/                ← ArgoCD apps
    ├── app-dev.yaml
    └── app-prod.yaml

              
✅ Simple · Easy to see code + config together

              
❌ ArgoCD re-syncs on every code commit, even non-K8s changes

            

            

              
🔀 Pattern 2: App-Config Repo (Recommended)

              
Separate repo for K8s configs. ArgoCD only watches this repo.

              
sre-autopilot/             ← app code repo
├── app/
│   └── main.py
└── Dockerfile

sre-autopilot-config/      ← config repo (ArgoCD watches this)
├── helm/
│   ├── Chart.yaml
│   ├── values.yaml
│   ├── values-dev.yaml
│   └── values-prod.yaml
├── argocd-apps/
│   ├── dev.yaml
│   └── prod.yaml
└── README.md

              
✅ Clean separation · ArgoCD syncs only on config change

              
✅ CI writes to config repo → ArgoCD picks up automatically

            

          

          

            🏆 For the SRE Auto-Pilot project: Use Pattern 2. The app code repo has the Dockerfile. GitHub Actions builds the image, updates image.tag in values-prod.yaml in the config repo, commits, and pushes. ArgoCD watches the config repo and auto-deploys within 3 minutes.
          

        








  

    
Module 03

    
ArgoCD Architecture — What Runs in Your Cluster

    
Five components, one reconciliation loop — all running inside your cluster

  


  

    
👶 ELI5

    
ArgoCD is 5 containers running inside your cluster. One watches Git. One clones the Git repo and turns templates into real YAML. One compares that YAML to what's actually deployed. One handles the web UI and CLI. One handles who's allowed to log in. That's the whole system.

  


  
  

    
🏗️ Architecture Overview

    

      

        📁
        Git Repository
        (GitHub / GitLab / Bitbucket)
      

      
↓ clone & render

      

        
ArgoCD (running in-cluster)

        

          

            
🌐

            
API Server

            
REST + gRPC
UI / CLI / Webhooks

          

          

            
📋

            
Repo Server

            
Clones repos
Renders Helm/Kustomize

          

          

            
🔄

            
App Controller

            
Reconciler loop
Diff + Sync

          

          

            
⚡

            
Redis

            
Cache layer
App state

          

          

            
🔑

            
Dex

            
SSO / OIDC
GitHub OAuth

          

        

      

      
↓ kubectl apply

      

        ☸️
        Kubernetes Cluster (target namespaces)
      

    

  


  
  

    
⚙️ Component Breakdown

    

      

        
ComponentRoleDevOps Analogy

        
          
API ServerREST + gRPC interface — serves the UI, argocd CLI, and CI webhook callsFastAPI entry point for your service

          
Repo ServerStateless — clones repos, renders manifests (Helm template, Kustomize build, plain YAML)Helm template rendering engine

          
App ControllerThe Kubernetes controller loop — watches cluster state, diffs against Git, triggers sync when OutOfSyncKubernetes reconciler (like Deployment controller)

          
RedisCaches app state, rendered manifests, cluster info — reduces Git/API callsIn-memory cache layer

          
DexOIDC identity provider — GitHub OAuth, LDAP, SAML, Microsoft ADOAuth2 proxy / identity broker

        
      

    

  


  
  

    
🚀 Installation (5 minutes)

    
BashInstall ArgoCD

    
# 1. Create namespace
kubectl create namespace argocd

# 2. Apply official manifests
kubectl apply -n argocd -f \
  https://raw.githubusercontent.com/argoproj/argo-cd/stable/manifests/install.yaml

# 3. Wait for all pods ready (~60s)
kubectl wait --for=condition=Ready pod --all \
  -n argocd --timeout=120s

# 4. Get initial admin password
argocd admin initial-password -n argocd

# 5. Port-forward UI for local access
kubectl port-forward svc/argocd-server \
  -n argocd 8080:443
# → Open https://localhost:8080  (user: admin)

  


  
  

    
⌨️ argocd CLI Quick Reference

    
BashEssential ArgoCD commands

    
# Authentication
argocd login localhost:8080 --insecure

# Application management
argocd app list                        # List all apps
argocd app get payments-api            # Full details + health
argocd app diff payments-api           # What would change
argocd app sync payments-api           # Trigger sync now
argocd app wait payments-api --health  # Wait until Healthy

# History & rollback
argocd app history payments-api        # All revisions
argocd app rollback payments-api 3     # Rollback to revision 3

# Troubleshooting
argocd app logs payments-api           # Pod logs via ArgoCD
argocd admin settings validate         # Check config

Module 04

    
ArgoCD Applications — The Core CRD

    
Every deployment starts with an Application YAML — the CRD that connects Git to your cluster

  


  

    
👶 ELI5

    
An ArgoCD Application is a YAML file that says: "Watch this Git repo at this path, and keep this Kubernetes namespace in sync with it." That's all. One Application = one microservice. ArgoCD reads this YAML and does all the work.

  


  
  

    
📱 Annotated Application YAML

    
YAMLpayments-api Application

    
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: Application              # ArgoCD custom resource
metadata:
  name: payments-api
  namespace: argocd            # Always lives in argocd namespace
spec:
  project: production          # RBAC boundary (ArgoCD Project)

  source:
    repoURL: https://github.com/myorg/k8s-config
    targetRevision: HEAD       # Branch / tag / commit SHA
    path: apps/payments-api    # Folder with K8s manifests

    # --- For Helm charts, replace path with: ---
    # chart: payments-api
    # helm:
    #   valueFiles: [values.yaml, values-prod.yaml]

  destination:
    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc  # In-cluster target
    namespace: production

  syncPolicy:
    automated:
      selfHeal: true    # Revert manual kubectl changes
      prune: true       # Delete K8s resources removed from Git
    syncOptions:
      - CreateNamespace=true   # Auto-create namespace
      - ServerSideApply=true   # Use server-side apply

  


  
  

    

      
🔁 Sync Status

      
Does Git match the cluster?

      

        
✅ Synced — Git and cluster match perfectly

        
⚠️ OutOfSync — Cluster differs from Git

        
🔄 Syncing — Applying changes right now

        
❓ Unknown — Can't determine sync state

      

    

    

      
❤️ Health Status

      
Is the deployed app working?

      

        
🟢 Healthy — All resources running fine

        
🟡 Progressing — Rollout in progress

        
🔴 Degraded — Pod crashing / unavailable

        
⏸️ Suspended — App paused manually

        
🚫 Missing — In Git but not in cluster

      

    

  


  

    
💡 Critical Insight

    
You can be Synced but Degraded. The YAML was applied successfully, but the pod is CrashLoopBackOff. Sync ≠ Healthy. Always check both statuses.

  


  
  

    
🎮 Interactive: Health State Explorer

    
Click any state to see what causes it and how to fix it:

    

      
      
      
      
      
      
    

    

      
    

  


  
  

    
🌳 App-of-Apps Pattern

    
Scale to 50 services without losing your mind

    
Problem: 30 microservices = 30 Application YAMLs to manage, update, and troubleshoot individually.

    
Solution: One "root" Application that watches a Git folder full of Application YAMLs — and creates them all automatically.

    

      

        🌳
        root-app (Application)
        ↓ watches /argocd-apps/ in Git
      

      

        
📱 payments-api.yaml (Application CRD)

        
📱 auth-service.yaml (Application CRD)

        
📱 frontend.yaml (Application CRD)

        
📱 ... 27 more services

      

    

    

# Git repo structure for App-of-Apps:
argocd-apps/
├── payments-api.yaml   ← kind: Application
├── auth-service.yaml   ← kind: Application
├── frontend.yaml       ← kind: Application
└── ...

# Root Application just points here:
spec.source.path: argocd-apps/
# ArgoCD creates all child Apps automatically

  


  
  

    
⚡ ApplicationSet — Next Level

    
Instead of writing 30 Application YAMLs, write ONE ApplicationSet with a template and a generator. ArgoCD creates all Applications automatically.

    
YAMLApplicationSet with git-directory generator

    
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: ApplicationSet
metadata:
  name: all-services
spec:
  generators:
  - git:
      repoURL: https://github.com/myorg/k8s-config
      revision: HEAD
      directories:
      - path: apps/*         # Every folder = one Application
  template:
    metadata:
      name: '{{path.basename}}'  # app name = folder name
    spec:
      source:
        path: '{{path}}'
        repoURL: https://github.com/myorg/k8s-config
      destination:
        server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
        namespace: production

  








  

    
Module 05

    
Sync Policies — Auto-Heal, Prune & Waves

    
Make your cluster self-healing — and know exactly when not to

  


  
  

    
🔁 Manual vs Auto-Sync

    

      

        
Manual SyncAuto-Sync

        
          
When to useProduction — human approval gates requiredDev / staging — deploy on every commit

          
Triggered byargocd app sync or UI clickArgoCD polls Git every ~3 min (or webhook)

          
selfHealDisabled — manual changes surviveEnabled — manual changes reverted

          
pruneDisabled — deleted Git resources keptEnabled — resources removed from Git get deleted

          
RiskDrift builds up if nobody runs syncPrune can delete resources if Git has a typo

        
      

    

  


  
  

    

      
🛡️ selfHeal: true

      
Someone runs kubectl scale or kubectl apply manually. ArgoCD detects the drift and reverts it on the next reconciliation cycle.

      

syncPolicy:
  automated:
    selfHeal: true
# Result:
# kubectl scale deploy myapp --replicas=1
# ArgoCD: "OutOfSync detected"
# ArgoCD: "kubectl apply → replicas: 3 restored"

    

    

      
⚠️ prune: true

      
You remove a resource from Git (e.g., an old ConfigMap). ArgoCD deletes it from the cluster. Powerful — but dangerous if a YAML file has a typo.

      

syncPolicy:
  automated:
    prune: true
# ⚠️ Warning: test prune in dev first.
# If a valid manifest is accidentally
# excluded from Git, ArgoCD will delete
# the K8s resource from the cluster.

    

  


  
  

    
🔄 Sync Phases & Hooks

    

      

        
PhaseWhen it runsCommon use cases

        
          
PreSyncBefore any resources are appliedDB migrations, backups, schema validation

          
SyncMain resource apply (Deployments, Services, etc.)Everything else — the normal deploy

          
PostSyncAfter all resources are healthySmoke tests, cache warm-up, Slack notifications

          
SyncFailIf the sync failsAlert on-call team, trigger rollback procedure

        
      

    

    
YAMLPreSync DB migration hook

    
apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: db-migrate
  annotations:
    argocd.argoproj.io/hook: PreSync           # Run before apply
    argocd.argoproj.io/hook-delete-policy: HookSucceeded
    argocd.argoproj.io/sync-wave: "-1"       # Before wave 0
spec:
  template:
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: migrate
        image: myapp:v2.0.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate"]

  


  
  

    
🌊 Sync Waves — Ordering Resources

    
Within a sync phase, waves control order. Lower wave number applies first. Use to ensure namespaces and RBAC exist before workloads.

    

      
wave: -1Namespace creation

      
→

      
wave: 0RBAC + ServiceAccounts

      
→

      
wave: 1ConfigMaps + Secrets

      
→

      
wave: 2Deployments + Services

    

    

metadata:
  annotations:
    argocd.argoproj.io/sync-wave: "2"  # Deploy after RBAC is ready

  


  
  

    
🚫 Sync Windows — Deploy Freezes

    
Block all syncs during maintenance windows, high-traffic periods, or change freezes.

    
YAMLNo deploys on Friday evenings

    
spec:
  syncWindows:
  - kind: deny
    schedule: "0 17 * * 5"    # Fridays 5pm
    duration: 3h
    applications:
    - "*"                    # All apps
    namespaces:
    - production
  - kind: allow
    schedule: "0 2 * * 1-5"   # Weekdays 2am
    duration: 2h              # Maintenance window
    applications:
    - "*"

  


  
  

    
🎮 Interactive: Sync Lifecycle

    
Step through the complete lifecycle — git push to self-healed:

    

      

        

          
Step 1 / 6

          

          

            App Status:
            
          

          

        

      

      

        
        
      

    

  


        
        

          
🚨 When Things Go Wrong — ArgoCD Troubleshooting Guide

          
ArgoCD will show you what is wrong. Here's how to fix the most common problems a new user hits:


          


            

              

                SYNC FAILED
                ComparisonError: failed to get cluster info
              

              
Cause: ArgoCD can't reach the target cluster. Usually a network/cert issue or the cluster was rebuilt.

              
argocd cluster list                    # Is the cluster registered?
argocd cluster get https://k8s.svc    # Show cluster connection status
kubectl get pods -n argocd             # Are ArgoCD pods running?

            


            

              

                SYNC FAILED
                helm template failed: error converting YAML to JSON
              

              
Cause: Your Helm templates have a YAML syntax error. ArgoCD can't render the manifests.

              
# Test locally before pushing to Git:
helm template my-release ./helm-chart --values values-prod.yaml
# Also lint the chart:
helm lint ./helm-chart

            


            

              

                DEGRADED
                Synced ✅ but Degraded 💔 — Pod CrashLoopBackOff
              

              
Cause: ArgoCD applied the manifests correctly, but the app is crashing. This is an app bug, not ArgoCD issue.

              
# Get pod details:
kubectl get pods -n production
kubectl describe pod <pod-name> -n production   # Events section
kubectl logs <pod-name> -n production --previous # Last crash logs
# In ArgoCD UI: click the Deployment → click the Pod → "Logs" tab

            


            

              

                STUCK OUTOFSYNC
                App keeps flipping OutOfSync even after sync
              

              
Cause: An external controller (HPA, admission webhook, operator) is modifying the resource after ArgoCD applies it. Classic "drift loop."

              
# See the actual diff causing OutOfSync:
argocd app diff my-app
# Common fix: use ignoreDifferences in Application YAML:
spec:
  ignoreDifferences:
  - group: apps
    kind: Deployment
    jsonPointers:
    - /spec/replicas   # HPA manages replicas — ignore this field

            


            

              

                SYNC FAILED
                ProgressDeadlineExceeded — rollout stuck
              

              
Cause: The new pods can't start within the deadline (600s default). New image broken, resource limits too low, or node doesn't have capacity.

              
# Roll back immediately while you investigate:
argocd app rollback my-app
# Check what happened to new pods:
kubectl describe deployment my-app -n production
kubectl get events -n production --sort-by='.lastTimestamp'

            


          

          

            💡 Golden debug rule: Start in the ArgoCD UI → click the red/orange resource → read the Events tab → then go to kubectl. 90% of issues are visible in the UI without any CLI commands.
          

        








  

    
Module 06

    
RBAC, Projects & Security

    
Who can sync what, to where — and how to keep secrets out of Git

  


  
  

    
🗂️ ArgoCD Projects — Isolation Boundaries

    
An ArgoCD Project is a namespace isolation + access control boundary for a team. Team A's apps can only deploy to Team A's namespaces from Team A's repos — even if they have ArgoCD access.

    
YAMLAppProject for the payments team

    
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: AppProject
metadata:
  name: payments-team
  namespace: argocd
spec:
  description: "Payments team — production namespace"

  # Only allow from these repos
  sourceRepos:
  - 'https://github.com/myorg/payments-*'

  # Only allow deploying to these namespaces
  destinations:
  - namespace: payments-production
    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
  - namespace: payments-staging
    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc

  # Block dangerous cluster-level resources
  clusterResourceBlacklist:
  - group: ''
    kind: Node
  - group: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
    kind: ClusterRole

  


  
  

    
🔐 RBAC Policy Syntax

    
RBACargocd-rbac-cm ConfigMap

    
# Policy format: p, subject, resource, action, object, effect
# Subjects: role:name or user email or group
# Resources: applications, clusters, repositories, projects
# Actions: get, create, update, delete, sync, override, action

p, role:devops, applications, sync,   */*, allow
p, role:devops, applications, get,    */*, allow
p, role:devops, applications, delete, */*, deny    # No deletes!

p, role:readonly, applications, get,  */*, allow
p, role:readonly, applications, sync, */*, deny

# Assign users to roles
g, alice@company.com, role:devops
g, ops-team,          role:devops     # SSO group
g, bob@company.com,   role:readonly

  


  
  

    
🔒 Secrets — Never Store Plaintext in Git

    
The biggest ArgoCD mistake: putting password: mysecret in values.yaml and pushing to Git. Here are the production-safe alternatives:

    

      

        
ApproachToolHow it worksBest for

        
          
Vault PluginArgoCD Vault Plugin (AVP)Replaces <path:vault/data/prod#key> placeholders at sync time✅ HashiCorp Vault users

          
External SecretsESO + AWS SM / GCP SMK8s operator syncs secrets from cloud secret stores as K8s Secrets✅ Cloud-native teams

          
Sealed SecretsBitnami SealedSecretsEncrypt secrets with cluster-specific key, store encrypted YAML in Git✅ Simple, K8s native

          
SOPSMozilla SOPS + Age/KMSEncrypt YAML values in Git, decrypt at sync time✅ Helm chart teams

          
❌ Plaintextvalues.yamlSecrets visible in Git history forever❌ Never in production

        
      

    

  


  
  

    
🔑 SSO Setup — GitHub OAuth via Dex

    
YAMLargocd-cm ConfigMap — GitHub OAuth

    
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: argocd-cm
  namespace: argocd
data:
  url: https://argocd.mycompany.com

  dex.config: |
    connectors:
    - type: github
      id: github
      name: GitHub
      config:
        clientID: $GITHUB_CLIENT_ID
        clientSecret: $GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET
        orgs:
        - name: myorg           # Restrict to your GitHub org
          teams:
          - devops-team
          - platform-team

  


  
  

    
✅ Security Checklist

    

      
✅ Enable SSO (Dex + GitHub/OIDC) — disable local users in prod

      
✅ Create ArgoCD Projects per team — restrict source repos and destinations

      
✅ Use role:readonly for developers — only DevOps/SRE gets sync permission

      
✅ Never use the default project in production — always create named projects

      
✅ Use Sealed Secrets / ESO — no plaintext secrets in Git, ever

      
✅ Enable argocd-notifications for sync failures and degraded apps

      
✅ Set resource limits on ArgoCD components — it runs in prod cluster

      
⚠️ Rotate admin password after initial setup — or disable it entirely

    

  








  

    
Module 07 · Connecting the Dots

    
Helm + ArgoCD — Best of Both Worlds

    
Use ArgoCD to continuously deliver your Helm charts — no manual helm upgrade ever again

  


  

    
👶 Why this combination wins

    
Helm gives you templating power — one chart, many environments. ArgoCD gives you GitOps delivery — git push = deployed, drift-detected, audited. Together: every helm upgrade is a git commit, every rollback is a git revert, and your cluster is always as-declared-in-Git.

  


  
  

    
📱 ArgoCD Application — Helm Source

    
YAMLApplication pointing to a Helm chart

    
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: Application
metadata:
  name: payments-api-prod
  namespace: argocd
spec:
  source:
    repoURL: https://github.com/myorg/k8s-config
    targetRevision: main
    path: charts/payments-api   # Helm chart directory in Git

    helm:
      releaseName: payments-api  # Override Release.Name
      valueFiles:
        - values.yaml            # Base values (always applied)
        - values-production.yaml # Env override (higher priority)
      values: |                  # Inline values (highest priority)
        image:
          tag: "v2.1.0"

  destination:
    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
    namespace: production

  


  
  

    
📁 Values File Strategy — One Chart, Many Environments

    

# Git repo layout — one chart, two ArgoCD Applications:
charts/payments-api/
├── Chart.yaml
├── templates/
├── values.yaml              ← base defaults (always read)
├── values-staging.yaml      ← staging ArgoCD App adds this
└── values-production.yaml   ← prod ArgoCD App adds this

    

      

        
🔵 Staging App

        

helm:
  valueFiles:
    - values.yaml
    - values-staging.yaml
  # replicas: 1, debug: true,
  # image.tag: latest

      

      

        
🟠 Production App

        

helm:
  valueFiles:
    - values.yaml
    - values-production.yaml
  # replicas: 5, debug: false,
  # image.tag: v2.1.0

      

    

  


  
  

    
📦 ArgoCD Source Types

    

      

        
ModeConfigNotes

        
          
Helm chart in Gitpath: charts/myappFull chart lives in repo — most flexible

          
Helm from registrychart: myapp + repoURL: oci://ArgoCD pulls from ArtifactHub/Bitnami

          
Kustomizekustomize: blockPatch-based overlays over base manifests

          
Plain YAMLpath: manifests/Just apply all files in folder

          
Jsonnetdirectory.jsonnet:For Jsonnet-based config generation

        
      

    

  


  
  

    
⚠️ Common Gotchas: Helm + ArgoCD

    

      
Release.Name mismatch: By default ArgoCD sets Release.Name = Application name. Always set helm.releaseName explicitly to avoid surprise name changes.

      
helm diff vs argocd app diff: The helm diff plugin doesn't work with ArgoCD's server-side rendering. Use argocd app diff myapp instead.

      
Hooks fire twice: If your Helm chart has hooks AND you configure ArgoCD sync hooks, both fire. Be careful of duplicate DB migrations or smoke tests.

      
helm test doesn't run: helm test commands don't execute via ArgoCD. Use a PostSync hook Job instead.

      
Sensitive values in inline values: The values: block in Application YAML is stored in the cluster as plaintext. Use Sealed Secrets or ESO for anything sensitive.

    

  


  
  

    
🔄 End-to-End GitOps Flow

    

      

        
1

        

          Developer edits values-production.yaml
          Changes image.tag: v2.1.0 → creates PR → approved → merged to main
        

      

      
↓

      

        
2

        

          ArgoCD detects the commit
          Polls every 3 min or webhook triggered → OutOfSync detected
        

      

      
↓

      

        
3

        

          Repo Server renders the chart
          Runs helm template payments-api ./charts -f values.yaml -f values-production.yaml
        

      

      
↓

      

        
4

        

          App Controller diffs + applies
          kubectl apply with only the changed resources — rolling update begins
        

      

      
↓

      

        
✅

        

          Synced + Healthy
          Deployment complete. Zero manual helm upgrade. Full Git audit trail.
        

      

    

  


        
        

          
🤖 GitHub Actions → ArgoCD: The Complete CI/CD Pipeline

          
The most common real-world pattern: CI (GitHub Actions) builds and tags the image → writes the new tag to Git → ArgoCD detects the Git change → deploys automatically. Here's the exact workflow for the SRE Auto-Pilot:


          
Step 1 — CI: Build & Push Image (app code repo)

          
# .github/workflows/build.yml  (in sre-autopilot/ repo)
name: Build and Deploy
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Build & push Docker image
        uses: docker/build-push-action@v5
        with:
          push: true
          tags: ghcr.io/myorg/sre-autopilot:${{ github.sha }}

      # This is the KEY step — update image tag in the CONFIG repo
      - name: Update image tag in config repo
        run: |
          git clone https://x-access-token:${{ secrets.CONFIG_REPO_TOKEN }}@github.com/myorg/sre-autopilot-config
          cd sre-autopilot-config
          # Use yq or sed to update the tag in values-prod.yaml
          yq e -i '.image.tag = "${{ github.sha }}"' helm/values-prod.yaml
          git config user.email "ci@myorg.com"
          git config user.name "CI Bot"
          git commit -am "ci: bump image tag to ${{ github.sha }}"
          git push


          
Step 2 — ArgoCD: Auto-detects the Git change (config repo)

          

            

              ArgoCD polls every 3 min
              OR configure a webhook for instant detection
            

            

              ArgoCD sees: values-prod.yaml changed → image.tag: abc123 → new version

              App status → OutOfSync → ArgoCD runs: helm template → kubectl apply

              Deployment rollout starts → pods updated → App status → Synced ✅ Healthy ✅
            

          


          
Step 3 — Webhook (optional but recommended for instant deploys)

          
# In sre-autopilot-config repo → Settings → Webhooks → Add webhook
Payload URL: https://your-argocd.company.com/api/webhook
Content type: application/json
Secret: (set same as argocd-secret webhook.github.secret)
Events: Just the push event ✅

# ArgoCD argocd-cm ConfigMap - enable webhook processing:
data:
  webhook.github.secret: "your-webhook-secret"


          

            
🔄 Complete Flow — End to End

            

              
1Developer merges PR to main in app code repo

              
2GitHub Actions: builds ghcr.io/myorg/sre-autopilot:abc123, pushes to GHCR

              
3GitHub Actions: clones config repo, yq updates image.tag in values-prod.yaml, pushes commit

              
4Git webhook fires → ArgoCD notified instantly (no 3-min wait)

              
5ArgoCD Repo Server clones config repo, runs helm template with new tag

              
6App Controller diffs rendered YAML vs cluster → OutOfSync → triggers sync

              
7kubectl apply → rolling update → new pods up → old pods terminated → Synced ✅ Healthy ✅

              
8Slack notification: "sre-autopilot-prod deployed abc123 — Synced ✅ · 2m 14s"

Module 09 · Build It

    
Real ArgoCD Projects

    
Four progressively complex GitOps projects to build, ship, and add to your DevOps portfolio

  




          

            ⛵
            

              
GitOps the SRE Auto-Pilot — Full Walkthrough

              

                ArgoCD
                Helm
                Multi-env
                GitHub Actions
                GitOps
              

            

            Intermediate
          

          
Take the AI SRE Auto-Pilot project (FastAPI + Redis + Postgres) and deploy it entirely via ArgoCD. This walkthrough shows you every file you need to create — not just a roadmap.


          

            
📁 Step 1 — Create the Config Repo Structure

            
sre-autopilot-config/           ← new dedicated Git repo
├── helm/
│   ├── Chart.yaml
│   ├── values.yaml             ← base defaults
│   ├── values-dev.yaml         ← dev overrides
│   ├── values-prod.yaml        ← prod overrides (CI writes image.tag here)
│   └── templates/
│       ├── deployment.yaml
│       ├── service.yaml
│       └── ingress.yaml
└── argocd-apps/
    ├── sre-dev.yaml            ← ArgoCD Application for dev
    └── sre-prod.yaml           ← ArgoCD Application for prod

          


          

            
📄 Step 2 — Chart.yaml

            
apiVersion: v2
name: sre-autopilot
description: AI SRE Auto-Pilot — FastAPI + LangGraph + Redis + Postgres
type: application
version: 1.0.0        # chart version — bump when chart structure changes
appVersion: "1.0.0"   # app version — CI will update this to image tag

          


          

            
📄 Step 3 — values.yaml (base defaults)

            
# helm/values.yaml — default values, safe for dev
fastapi:
  image:
    repository: ghcr.io/myorg/sre-autopilot
    tag: "latest"          # CI will overwrite this in values-prod.yaml
    pullPolicy: IfNotPresent
  replicas: 1
  port: 8000
  env:
    ENVIRONMENT: "development"
    LOG_LEVEL: "debug"

redis:
  enabled: true
  image: redis:7-alpine
  port: 6379

postgres:
  enabled: true
  image: postgres:15-alpine
  port: 5432
  database: sre_db
  user: sre_user

ingress:
  enabled: false          # disabled in dev, enabled in prod overlay
  host: ""

          


          

            
📄 Step 4 — values-prod.yaml (production overlay — CI writes image.tag here)

            
# helm/values-prod.yaml — production overrides
fastapi:
  image:
    tag: "abc1234"         # ← CI (GitHub Actions) writes the git SHA here on every build
  replicas: 3              # scale up for prod
  env:
    ENVIRONMENT: "production"
    LOG_LEVEL: "info"

ingress:
  enabled: true
  host: sre-autopilot.company.com

postgres:
  resources:
    requests:
      memory: "256Mi"
      cpu: "250m"

          


          

            
📄 Step 5 — ArgoCD Application YAML for prod (argocd-apps/sre-prod.yaml)

            
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: Application
metadata:
  name: sre-autopilot-prod
  namespace: argocd
spec:
  project: default
  source:
    repoURL: https://github.com/myorg/sre-autopilot-config
    targetRevision: main
    path: helm                           # folder with the Helm chart
    helm:
      releaseName: sre-autopilot
      valueFiles:
        - values.yaml                    # base
        - values-prod.yaml               # prod overrides (has the image tag)
  destination:
    server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
    namespace: production
  syncPolicy:
    automated:
      selfHeal: true                     # revert any manual kubectl changes
      prune: true                        # delete resources removed from Git
    syncOptions:
      - CreateNamespace=true

          


          

            
📄 Step 6 — Apply the Application to the cluster

            
# One-time bootstrap — apply the Application YAML
kubectl apply -f argocd-apps/sre-prod.yaml -n argocd

# Watch ArgoCD pick it up:
argocd app list
argocd app get sre-autopilot-prod

# Trigger first sync manually (then it auto-syncs forever after):
argocd app sync sre-autopilot-prod

          


          

            
🔄 Step 7 — GitHub Actions: auto-update image tag on every merge to main

            
# .github/workflows/deploy.yml in sre-autopilot/ (app code repo)
name: Build & GitOps Deploy
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]
jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - name: Build image
        run: docker build -t ghcr.io/myorg/sre-autopilot:${{ github.sha }} .
      - name: Push image
        run: docker push ghcr.io/myorg/sre-autopilot:${{ github.sha }}
      - name: Update config repo image tag
        run: |
          git clone https://x-access-token:${{ secrets.CONFIG_TOKEN }}@github.com/myorg/sre-autopilot-config
          cd sre-autopilot-config
          # Update the image tag — ArgoCD will detect this Git change and deploy
          sed -i 's|tag: ".*"|tag: "${{ github.sha }}"|' helm/values-prod.yaml
          git commit -am "ci: deploy ${{ github.sha }}"
          git push

          


          

            
✅ What you now have after these 7 steps:

            

              
🔀 Every merge to main → automatic deploy to production in ~3 minutes

              
📜 Full audit trail: who deployed what, when, with a git SHA and PR link

              
🔁 Self-healing: someone runs kubectl scale manually → ArgoCD reverts it

              
⏮️ Rollback: argocd app rollback sre-autopilot-prod 3 — back in 30 seconds

              
🔍 Disaster recovery: kubectl apply -f argocd-apps/sre-prod.yaml → entire app rebuilt

            

          

        


  

    

      🌳
      

        
Multi-Environment App-of-Apps

        
App-of-AppsApplicationSet3 environments

      

      Intermediate
    

    
Build an App-of-Apps structure managing 5 microservices across 3 environments (dev/staging/prod). Use ApplicationSet with a git-directory generator to auto-onboard new services from a folder.

    

      Architecture:
      
root-app (Application) → watches /argocd-apps/prod/ in Git → creates child apps for payments, auth, frontend, notifications, gateway → each deploys to prod namespace

    

    

      4-step Roadmap:
      
    
        
  1. Create /argocd-apps/ folder structure in Git (dev, staging, prod subfolders)
    2. 
        
  2. Create root Application pointing to /argocd-apps/prod/
    3. 
        
  3. Add child Application YAMLs for each service into Git
    4. 
        
  4. Replace manual Application YAMLs with a single ApplicationSet and git-directory generator
    5.

      🏗️
      

        
ArgoCD + Crossplane Full GitOps

        
CrossplaneInfrastructure as CodeAdvanced

      

      Advanced
    

    
Use ArgoCD to manage Crossplane XR compositions — provisioning cloud infrastructure (RDS, S3, VPC) via git commit. Both code and infrastructure driven entirely by Git, zero AWS console clicks.

    

      Architecture:
      
git commit (RDS XR spec) → ArgoCD syncs Crossplane XR → Crossplane provisions RDS on AWS → connection secret injected into cluster → app deployment uses it

🔌 MCP Deep Dive

  
Master Model Context Protocol

  
The open standard that connects AI to everything — databases, repos, APIs, and your own tools. Build once, use with any AI.

Module 01

  
What is MCP?

  
The open protocol that makes AI stop reinventing integrations — released by Anthropic, Nov 2024. Now adopted by OpenAI and Google DeepMind.


  

    
🧠 ELI5 — The USB-C Analogy

    
MCP is the USB-C of AI tools. Before USB-C, every device had a different charger — nightmare. USB-C standardized it all. Before MCP, every AI tool needed custom code to talk to every data source. MCP standardizes how AI connects to everything. Write one MCP server for your Bitbucket instance and any AI that speaks MCP can use it instantly.

  


  

    
⚡ The N×M Problem — Before and After MCP

    

      

        
❌ Before MCP: N×M integrations

        
5 data sources × 3 AI tools = 15 custom integrations. Each one had different auth, different error handling, duplicate code. Change one API and 3 integrations break.

        

          Claude → GitHub (custom)

          Claude → Postgres (custom)

          Claude → Jira (custom)

          GPT-4 → GitHub (custom)

          GPT-4 → Postgres (custom)

          GPT-4 → Jira (custom)

          ... 9 more ...
        

      

      

        
✅ After MCP: N+M integrations

        
5 data sources × 1 MCP standard = 5 MCP servers. Any AI that speaks MCP connects to all 5 instantly. Build once, use everywhere.

        

          Any AI → MCP Client → GitHub MCP

          Any AI → MCP Client → Postgres MCP

          Any AI → MCP Client → Jira MCP

          Add a new AI? Zero new integrations.
Add a new tool? One MCP server.
        

      

    

  


  

    
📅 Timeline — How We Got Here

    

      

        
2023

        
Function calling — LLMs can call tools, but schemas are baked into every single API request. No standardization. Every provider did it differently.

      

      

        
Nov 2024

        
Anthropic releases MCP as an open standard. Tools are described once per session (not per request). Claude Desktop ships with MCP support out of the box.

      

      

        
Early 2025

        
OpenAI and Google DeepMind adopt MCP. Cursor, Windsurf, VS Code Copilot, and LangGraph all add native MCP support. 100+ official MCP servers published.

      

      

        
2025+

        
MCP becomes the de-facto standard for AI tool integration. Every major enterprise SaaS (Atlassian, AWS, Slack) ships an official MCP server.

      

    

  


  

    
🐳 DevOps Analogies — You Already Know This

    

      

        🐳 MCP is like Docker

        Docker standardized app packaging — "build once, run anywhere". MCP standardizes AI tool integration — "build once, use with any AI".
      

      

        📡 MCP is like HTTP

        HTTP is a protocol, not a product. Anyone can implement it. MCP is the same — an open spec. Any AI provider, any tool vendor can implement it.
      

      

        🔌 MCP is like a K8s Operator

        An Operator defines how a system behaves and reconciles state. An MCP server defines what an AI can do and executes actions on its behalf.
      

      

        📦 MCP is like npm/PyPI

        Instead of writing code to use a library, you install an MCP server. Your AI gets all the tools instantly — no integration code required.
      

    

  


  

    
✅ Why MCP Wins — Six Key Advantages

    

      
🏗️
Standardization
Build once, works with Claude, ChatGPT, LangGraph, Cursor — any MCP-compatible AI.

      
🔒
Security
Tools run locally on your machine. Your API keys and credentials never leave your network.

      
🧩
Composability
Mix filesystem + GitHub + Postgres in one agent. Each server is independent and pluggable.

      
⚡
Token Efficiency
Tools are discovered once per session via tools/list, not repeated in every single LLM request.

      
🔄
Dynamic Updates
Servers can notify clients when tools change at runtime — no restart needed.

      
🌍
Ecosystem
100+ ready-made servers for common tools. Don't build what already exists.

    

  







  
Module 02

  
Core Concepts

  
Three participants, three primitives — that's all you need to understand MCP completely.


  

    
🍽️ ELI5 — The Restaurant Model

    
Think of a restaurant. The Host is the restaurant manager (Claude Desktop or your app) — responsible for everything. The Client is a waiter who knows exactly one kitchen. The Server is a kitchen that specializes in one type of food (file system, GitHub, Postgres). The manager can have multiple waiters, each connecting to a different kitchen simultaneously.

  


  

    
👥 The Three Participants

    

      

        🖥️ HOST  — Claude Desktop / Your LangGraph Agent / Cursor IDE

        Manages the user interaction and owns all MCP Clients
        

          
🔗 Client 1
→ Filesystem

          
🔗 Client 2
→ GitHub

          
🔗 Client 3
→ Postgres

        

      

      
↕ JSON-RPC 2.0 (STDIO or HTTP)

      

        
📁 Filesystem
MCP Server

        
🐙 GitHub
MCP Server

        
🐘 Postgres
MCP Server

      

    

    

      
Host — the application the user runs. Creates and manages Clients. Has access to the LLM. Examples: Claude Desktop, your custom Python agent, Cursor.

      
Client — lives inside the Host. Maintains exactly one connection to one Server. Handles the JSON-RPC protocol. Usually invisible to you.

    

    
Server — a lightweight process that exposes tools and data. Can be local (stdin/stdout) or remote (HTTPS). You build these in Python with FastMCP.

  


  

    
🧩 The Three Primitives

    

      

        
ACTION

        
🔧 Tool

        What: Callable functions — the AI invokes these to do things.


        DevOps analogy: Like a kubectl command or REST API endpoint.


        Examples: list_pods(), create_pr(), query_db(), restart_service()
      

      

        
READ-ONLY

        
📄 Resource

        What: Read-only data — the AI reads this for context.


        DevOps analogy: Like a Prometheus metric, a log file, or a config file.


        Examples: system://info, db://schema, current cluster state
      

      

        
TEMPLATE

        
📝 Prompt

        What: Reusable interaction templates for structured tasks.


        DevOps analogy: Like a runbook or operational playbook.


        Examples: "Diagnose this service", "Review this PR", "Summarize incidents"
      

    

  


  

    
🔬 Advanced Features — Sampling & Elicitation

    

      

        Sampling

        A Server can ask the LLM "what should I do next?" — allows servers to request AI reasoning mid-execution. Example: your Bitbucket MCP server gets a complex PR diff and asks Claude to summarize it before posting a comment.
      

      

        Elicitation

        A Server can ask the user "is it OK to do X?" — enables human-in-the-loop approvals. Example: "This will restart the production pod. Are you sure?" before executing a destructive action.
      

    

  


  

    
🔍 Interactive Concept Explorer — See the JSON-RPC Messages

    

      
      
      
      
      
    

    
{"jsonrpc":"2.0","id":2,"method":"tools/list","params":{}}

    
Client asks: what tools do you have? This happens ONCE per session. The server returns all tool names, descriptions, and input schemas — much more token-efficient than repeating schemas in every LLM request.

  







  
Module 03

  
How MCP Works Under the Hood

  
JSON-RPC 2.0, two transports, five lifecycle steps. This is the entire protocol.


  

    
🧠 ELI5 — Very Formal Conversation

    
MCP uses JSON-RPC 2.0 — like HTTP but for function calls. Every message is JSON, every request gets a response. It's a very formal conversation: "Hello" → "I support X and Y" → "List tools" → "Here are my 6 tools" → "Call tool get_cpu_usage" → "CPU is 87%". That's it. Every MCP interaction follows this exact pattern.

  


  

    
🏗️ Architecture Diagram

    
HOST (Claude Desktop / LangGraph Agent)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  LLM (Claude)                           │
│    ↕ decides what to do based on tools  │
│  MCP Client                             │
│    ↕ JSON-RPC 2.0 messages              │
└──────────────┬──────────────────────────┘
               │
       Transport Layer
  (STDIO pipes  OR  Streamable HTTP/SSE)
               │
┌──────────────▼──────────────────────────┐
│  MCP SERVER (Your Python / Node process)│
│    list_repositories()                  │
│    get_pull_requests()                  │
│    get_pipeline_status()                │
│    create_pr_comment()                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘

  


  

    
🔄 5-Step Lifecycle — Step Through It

    

      

        
1

        
2

        
3

        
4

        
5

      

      

        
Step 1: Initialize

        
Client sends initialize — declares its MCP protocol version and capabilities. This is the handshake. Without this step, neither side knows what the other supports.

      

      

        
        
        Step 1 / 5
      

    

  


  

    
🚌 STDIO vs Streamable HTTP — Which Transport to Use?

    

      

        
STDIOStreamable HTTP

        
          
How it worksstdin/stdout pipes — like piping between Unix commandsHTTP POST requests + Server-Sent Events for streaming

          
Best forLocal tools: file system, local databases, CLI wrappersRemote/cloud APIs, SaaS tools, enterprise systems

          
AuthOS-level process isolation — most secureBearer tokens, OAuth 2.0

          
PerformanceFastest — no network overheadNetwork latency but horizontally scalable

          
Multi-clientOne client per processMultiple clients, load-balanced

          
When to useClaude Desktop, Cursor, local agents, your dev machineProduction enterprise APIs, shared team servers

          
ExampleFilesystem server, kubectl wrapper, local Bitbucket ServerOfficial Atlassian Remote MCP, AWS MCP, Slack MCP

        
      

    

  


  

    
📬 JSON-RPC Message Anatomy

    

      

        
Request (Client → Server)

        
{"jsonrpc": "2.0",
 "id": 3,
 "method": "tools/call",
 "params": {
   "name": "get_pipeline_status",
   "arguments": {
     "repository": "sre-autopilot",
     "limit": 5
   }
 }}

      

      

        
Response (Server → Client)

        
{"jsonrpc": "2.0",
 "id": 3,
 "result": {
   "content": [{
     "type": "text",
     "text": "[{\"build\":42,\"state\":\"SUCCESSFUL\",
       \"branch\":\"main\"}]"
   }]
 }}

      

    

    

      

        
Notification (Server → Client, no reply expected)

        
{"jsonrpc": "2.0",
 "method": "notifications/tools/list_changed"
 // No "id" field = notification, not a request
}

      

      

        
Error Response

        
{"jsonrpc": "2.0",
 "id": 3,
 "error": {
   "code": -32602,
   "message": "Invalid params",
   "data": {"missing": "repository"}
 }}

      

    

  







  
Module 04

  
Using MCP Today — No Coding Required

  
Connect 100+ ready-made servers to Claude Desktop in under 5 minutes. No code needed for most use cases.


  

    
🚀 Setup in 3 Steps

    

      

        
1️⃣

        Install Claude Desktop

        Download from claude.ai — available for Mac and Windows
      

      

        
2️⃣

        Edit claude_desktop_config.json

        Mac: ~/Library/Application Support/Claude/
Win: %APPDATA%/Claude/
      

      

        
3️⃣

        Restart Claude Desktop

        New tools appear automatically — ask Claude what it can do
      

    

  


  

    
🌐 Popular Official MCP Servers

    

      
📁 Filesystem
Read, write, and search local files and directories
"Find all .env files and check for hardcoded secrets"

      
🐙 GitHub
Issues, PRs, code search, Actions workflows
"List all open PRs with no review in 3+ days"

      
🐘 PostgreSQL
Run queries, inspect schema, analyze performance
"Show me the top 10 slowest queries from pg_stat"

      
🔍 Brave Search
Real-time web search without leaving Claude
"What CVEs affect OpenSSL 3.0.x this month?"

      
💬 Slack
Send messages, read channels, create threads
"Notify #deployments that prod deploy started"

      
☁️ AWS
EC2, S3, Lambda, RDS, CloudWatch management
"List all EC2 instances with no tags across all regions"

    

  


  

    
📄 Complete claude_desktop_config.json Example

    
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "filesystem": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem",
               "/Users/me/projects", "/tmp"]
      // Grants Claude read/write to these directories only
    },
    "github": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-github"],
      "env": {
        "GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN": "ghp_xxxxxxxxxxxx"
      }
    },
    "postgres": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-postgres",
               "postgresql://localhost/mydb"]
      // Connection string passed as argument
    }
  }
}

  


  

    
💬 What You Can Ask After Setup

    

      

        📋 Log Analysis: "Check if my app logs have any OOM errors in the last hour"

        → Filesystem MCP reads /var/log/app.log and searches for patterns
      

      

        🐙 PR Review: "Find all open PRs older than 3 days with no reviewer assigned"

        → GitHub MCP queries the repos, returns filtered list with author + date
      

      

        🐘 Database: "Query the users table and find accounts created in the last 24h"

        → Postgres MCP runs the query, Claude formats and explains the results
      

    

  


  

    
🔄 MCP vs Function Calling — What's the Difference?

    

      

        
Function CallingMCP

        
          
Tool discoverySchema sent in every single API requesttools/list called once per session

          
Token costHigh — tool schemas repeat every messageLow — schemas sent once, referenced by name

          
Multi-toolAll tools must be defined in each request100+ tools from multiple servers, all available

          
ServerBaked into your API call codeSeparate process — can be reused across apps

          
UpdatesRestart your app to add toolsServer sends list_changed notification — live updates

          
EcosystemProvider-specific — OpenAI format ≠ Anthropic formatUniversal — works with any MCP-compatible AI

          
Use whenSimple apps, one AI provider, few toolsProduction agents, multiple tools, reusable servers

        
      

    

  







  
Module 05

  
Build Your First MCP Server

  
From zero to a working server in 15 minutes using FastMCP — the FastAPI of MCP.


  

    
⚡ Why FastMCP?

    
FastMCP is to MCP what FastAPI is to REST APIs. You write Python functions. It handles the entire JSON-RPC protocol, message routing, capability negotiation, and error handling. You just add @mcp.tool() and you're done. No boilerplate, no manual JSON construction.

  


  

    
📦 Step 1 — Install FastMCP

    
pip install fastmcp psutil

  


  

    
🔧 Step 2 — Write Your First Server

    
# system_monitor.py
from fastmcp import FastMCP
import psutil, socket, json

mcp = FastMCP("system-monitor")   # Give your server a name

@mcp.tool()
def get_cpu_usage() -> str:
    """Get current CPU usage percentage.
    Use this when the user asks about CPU load or performance."""
    return f"CPU: {psutil.cpu_percent(interval=1)}%"

@mcp.tool()
def get_memory_usage() -> str:
    """Get current memory usage statistics."""
    mem = psutil.virtual_memory()
    return f"Memory: {mem.percent}% used ({mem.used/1e9:.1f}GB / {mem.total/1e9:.1f}GB)"

@mcp.tool()
def get_disk_usage(path: str = "/") -> str:
    """Get disk usage for a specific path.
    Args:
        path: The filesystem path to check (default: /)
    """
    disk = psutil.disk_usage(path)
    return f"Disk {path}: {disk.percent}% used ({disk.free/1e9:.1f}GB free)"

@mcp.tool()
def get_top_processes(sort_by: str = "cpu", limit: int = 5) -> str:
    """Get top processes sorted by CPU or memory usage.
    Args:
        sort_by: Sort by 'cpu' or 'memory'
        limit: Number of processes to return (default 5)
    """
    procs = []
    for p in psutil.process_iter(['pid', 'name', 'cpu_percent', 'memory_percent']):
        try: procs.append(p.info)
        except: pass
    key = 'cpu_percent' if sort_by == 'cpu' else 'memory_percent'
    procs.sort(key=lambda x: x.get(key, 0), reverse=True)
    return json.dumps(procs[:limit])

if __name__ == "__main__":
    mcp.run()   # Uses STDIO transport by default

  


  

    
📊 Step 3 — Add a Resource (Read-only Context)

    
# Add this to system_monitor.py
@mcp.resource("system://info")
def get_system_info() -> str:
    """Read-only system info — AI can read this for context without calling a tool."""
    return json.dumps({
        "hostname": socket.gethostname(),
        "cpu_count": psutil.cpu_count(),
        "platform": psutil.sys.platform if hasattr(psutil, 'sys') else "linux",
        "total_memory_gb": round(psutil.virtual_memory().total / 1e9, 1)
    })

  


  

    
🔬 Step 4 — Test With MCP Inspector

    
# Install the inspector globally
npm install -g @modelcontextprotocol/inspector

# Run the inspector against your server
npx @modelcontextprotocol/inspector python system_monitor.py

# Opens http://localhost:6274 — visual browser UI to:
# - See all your tools with their schemas
# - Call each tool and see the response
# - Check resources
# - Verify error handling

    

      💡 SRE Tip: Always test every tool with the Inspector before connecting to Claude Desktop. The Inspector shows the exact JSON-RPC messages — same as what the AI will send.
    

  


  

    
⚙️ Step 5 — Connect to Claude Desktop

    
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "system-monitor": {
      "command": "python",
      "args": ["/absolute/path/to/system_monitor.py"]
      // IMPORTANT: always use absolute paths — Claude Desktop
      // launches the process from its own working directory
    }
  }
}

    
Now restart Claude Desktop and ask: "What's the CPU usage on my machine?" — Claude will call get_cpu_usage() automatically.

  


  

    
📐 MCP Server Design Principles

    

      
✅ Clear tool descriptions — the LLM reads your docstrings to decide which tool to call. Bad docstrings = wrong tool calls.

      
✅ Flat input schemas — avoid deeply nested objects. Simple types (str, int, bool) work best. LLMs struggle with complex nested schemas.

      
✅ Structured errors — return {"error": "message", "suggestion": "try X instead"} rather than letting exceptions propagate. The LLM can act on error messages.

      
✅ Idempotency — same input should produce same result. Safe to retry if something goes wrong during the agent loop.

      
✅ Rate limiting — add time.sleep(0.5) between external API calls. Your server is called by an LLM in a loop — it will hammer APIs without this.

    

  







  
Module 06 · Connecting the Dots

  
MCP + LangGraph

  
Use langchain-mcp-adapters to connect any MCP server to your LangGraph agent — production-ready AI with real tools.


  

    
⚡ Why This Combination Is So Powerful

    

      

        LangGraph gives you:
        
    
          
  • The agent reasoning loop
    • 
          
  • State management between steps
    • 
          
  • Multi-step diagnostic flows
    • 
          
  • Human-in-the-loop approvals
    • 
          
  • Retries and error recovery
    • 
        

      

      

        MCP gives you:
        
    
          
  • Standardized tools — build once
    • 
          
  • 100+ ready servers (GitHub, Slack, AWS)
    • 
          
  • Build your own in 10 minutes
    • 
          
  • Credentials stay local
    • 
          
  • Works with any AI, not just LangGraph
    • 
        

      

    

    

      🚀 Together: A production-ready AI agent that can interact with any tool in your stack — from Bitbucket to Kubernetes to your own internal APIs.
    

  


  

    
📦 Installation

    
pip install langchain-mcp-adapters langchain-anthropic langgraph

  


  

    
💻 Complete LangGraph + MCP Agent

    
# mcp_agent.py
import asyncio, os
from langchain_mcp_adapters.client import MultiServerMCPClient
from langchain_anthropic import ChatAnthropic
from langgraph.prebuilt import create_react_agent

async def main():
    # Step 1: Configure which MCP servers to connect to
    mcp_config = {
        "filesystem": {
            "command": "npx",
            "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem", "/tmp", "/var/log"],
            "transport": "stdio"
        },
        "github": {
            "command": "npx",
            "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-github"],
            "env": {"GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN": os.getenv("GITHUB_TOKEN")},
            "transport": "stdio"
        }
    }

    # Step 2: Connect to servers and get all tools
    async with MultiServerMCPClient(mcp_config) as mcp:
        tools = await mcp.get_tools()
        print(f"✅ Loaded {len(tools)} tools from {len(mcp_config)} MCP servers")
        for t in tools: print(f"   • {t.name}")

        # Step 3: Create a LangGraph ReAct agent with MCP tools
        llm   = ChatAnthropic(model="claude-sonnet-4-6")
        agent = create_react_agent(llm, tools)

        # Step 4: Run it
        result = await agent.ainvoke({
            "messages": [{
                "role": "user",
                "content": "Check if there are any error logs in /var/log/app.log from the last hour"
            }]
        })

        print("\n📋 Agent Response:")
        print(result["messages"][-1].content)

asyncio.run(main())

  


  

    
🤖 Connecting to Your SRE Auto-Pilot

    
Replace manually-defined tools in your existing LangGraph SRE agent with MCP tools — all of them, from multiple servers, automatically.

    
# In your LangGraph SRE diagnostic agent (sre_autopilot/agent.py)
# BEFORE: manually defined tool functions in Python
# AFTER: replace with MCP config — all tools loaded automatically

mcp_config = {
    "filesystem": {
        "command": "npx",
        "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem",
                 "/var/log", "/etc/config"],
    },
    "github": {
        "command": "npx",
        "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-github"],
        "env": {"GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN": os.getenv("GITHUB_TOKEN")}
    },
    "system-monitor": {        # Your custom MCP server from Module 05
        "command": "python",
        "args": ["/opt/mcp/system_monitor.py"]
    },
    "bitbucket": {             # Your custom Bitbucket MCP from Module 07
        "command": "python",
        "args": ["/opt/mcp/bitbucket_mcp.py"],
        "env": {
            "BITBUCKET_HOST": os.getenv("BITBUCKET_HOST"),
            "BITBUCKET_TOKEN": os.getenv("BITBUCKET_TOKEN"),
            "BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE": os.getenv("BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE")
        }
    }
}
# All tools from all 4 servers → automatically available in your LangGraph agent

  


  

    
🔀 Multi-Server Agent Flow

    

      
👤 User
→
"My pod is crashing — what's wrong?"

      
🦜 LangGraph
→
Agent loop begins. Passes user message to LLM with list of available tools.

      
🧠 LLM
→
Decides: "I should read the pod logs." Requests tool call: read_file("/var/log/app.log")

      
🔌 MCP Client
→
Routes tool call to the Filesystem MCP server via STDIO

      
📁 FS Server
→
Reads the file, returns last 100 lines as tool result

      
🧠 LLM
→
Reads logs, sees OOMKilled. Decides to check recent commits: list_commits("sre-autopilot")

      
🐙 GH Server
→
Returns last 5 commits. LLM spots memory limit change in commit abc1234.

      
✅ Final Answer
→
"Pod is OOMKilled. Commit abc1234 reduced memory limit from 512Mi to 128Mi. Fix: revert the values.yaml change."

    

  


  

    
🛠️ Common LangGraph + MCP Patterns

    

      

        create_react_agent — Quick agents with automatic tool use. LLM decides when to call tools and when to stop. Best for open-ended diagnostic tasks.
        
agent = create_react_agent(llm, tools)
result = await agent.ainvoke({"messages": [...]}, config={"recursion_limit": 25})

      

      

        StateGraph — Multi-step flows with defined transitions. Best for structured SRE runbooks: diagnose → decide → remediate → verify.
        
graph = StateGraph(AgentState)
graph.add_node("diagnose", diagnose_node)
graph.add_node("remediate", remediate_node)
graph.add_conditional_edges("diagnose", should_remediate)

      

      

        interrupt() — Human-in-the-loop approval before destructive actions. Essential for production. "About to restart the pod — confirm?"
        
from langgraph.types import interrupt
approval = interrupt({"action": "restart_pod", "pod": pod_name})
if approval["confirmed"]: restart_pod(pod_name)

      

    

  







  
Module 07 · Build Your Own

  
Build a Custom MCP Server

  
Connect Bitbucket, Jira, Jenkins, or any internal tool to AI agents using the exact same pattern.


  

    
🤔 When to Build Your Own MCP Server

    

      
✅ No official server exists for your tool (e.g., internal monitoring system)

      
✅ You're on Bitbucket Server / Data Center (on-prem) — the official Atlassian server is cloud-only

      
✅ You need custom logic — e.g., combined operations across multiple APIs in a single tool

      
✅ You want to expose your own internal REST API to AI without building a full integration

    

  


  

    
☁️ Official Atlassian MCP vs Custom Python Server

    

      

        
Official Atlassian Remote MCP

        
    
          
  • Cloud-based — Atlassian hosts it
    • 
          
  • Works for Bitbucket Cloud, Jira, Confluence
    • 
          
  • One config block, no code needed
    • 
          
  • Connects via OAuth 2.0 to your Atlassian account
    • 
        

        
// claude_desktop_config.json
"atlassian": {
  "command": "npx",
  "args": ["-y",
    "@atlassian/mcp-atlassian",
    "--cloud"
  ]
}

      

      

        
Custom Python MCP Server

        
    
          
  • For Bitbucket Server / Data Center (on-prem)
    • 
          
  • Full control — custom filters, combined tools
    • 
          
  • Works with any internal REST API
    • 
          
  • Your credentials stay on your machine
    • 
        

        
# bitbucket_mcp.py
@mcp.tool()
def get_pull_requests(repo, state="OPEN"):
    """Get PRs from your internal BB"""
    r = requests.get(
      f"{BBHOST}/repos/{repo}/prs",
      headers=auth_headers()
    )
    return json.dumps(r.json())

      

    

  


  

    
🔑 Bitbucket Authentication — Which Method to Use?

    

      

        
MethodWhen to useCode

        
          
Personal Access Token ⭐Bitbucket Server/Data Center (on-prem). Recommended for production.{"Authorization": f"Bearer {token}"}

          
OAuth 2.0Bitbucket Cloud — production apps with user-level authBearer token from OAuth flow

          
App PasswordQuick prototyping only — deprecated June 2026HTTP Basic auth with base64

        
      

    

  


  

    
🛠️ Complete Bitbucket MCP Server — 6 Tools

    
# bitbucket_mcp.py
from fastmcp import FastMCP
import requests, os, json
from base64 import b64encode

mcp = FastMCP("bitbucket-mcp")

# ── Configuration from environment variables ──────────────────────
BBHOST    = os.getenv("BITBUCKET_HOST", "https://api.bitbucket.org/2.0")
WORKSPACE = os.getenv("BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE")

def auth_headers():
    """Build auth headers — tries Personal Access Token first, falls back to Basic."""
    token = os.getenv("BITBUCKET_TOKEN")
    if token:
        return {"Authorization": f"Bearer {token}"}
    user = os.getenv("BITBUCKET_USERNAME")
    pwd  = os.getenv("BITBUCKET_PASSWORD")
    creds = b64encode(f"{user}:{pwd}".encode()).decode()
    return {"Authorization": f"Basic {creds}"}

# ── Tool 1: List Repositories ─────────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def list_repositories(workspace: str = None, pagelen: int = 10) -> str:
    """List repositories in a Bitbucket workspace.
    Args:
        workspace: Workspace slug (uses env var BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE if not provided)
        pagelen: Number of repos to return (default 10)
    """
    ws = workspace or WORKSPACE
    r = requests.get(f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{ws}",
                     headers=auth_headers(),
                     params={"pagelen": pagelen}, timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    repos = [{"name": x["name"], "slug": x["slug"], "language": x.get("language")}
             for x in r.json().get("values", [])]
    return json.dumps(repos)

# ── Tool 2: Get Pull Requests ─────────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def get_pull_requests(repository: str, state: str = "OPEN") -> str:
    """Get pull requests for a Bitbucket repository.
    Args:
        repository: Repository slug (e.g., 'sre-autopilot')
        state: PR state — OPEN, MERGED, or DECLINED
    """
    r = requests.get(
        f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{WORKSPACE}/{repository}/pullrequests",
        headers=auth_headers(),
        params={"state": state}, timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    prs = [{"id": x["id"], "title": x["title"],
            "author": x["author"]["display_name"],
            "source": x["source"]["branch"]["name"],
            "created_on": x.get("created_on", "")[:10]}
           for x in r.json().get("values", [])]
    return json.dumps(prs)

# ── Tool 3: Get Pipeline Status ───────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def get_pipeline_status(repository: str, limit: int = 5) -> str:
    """Get recent pipeline runs for a repository.
    Args:
        repository: Repository slug
        limit: Number of pipeline runs to return (default 5)
    """
    r = requests.get(
        f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{WORKSPACE}/{repository}/pipelines",
        headers=auth_headers(),
        params={"pagelen": limit}, timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    pipes = [{"build": x.get("build_number"),
              "state": x["state"]["name"],
              "result": x["state"].get("result", {}).get("name", ""),
              "branch": x.get("target", {}).get("branch", {}).get("name", "")}
             for x in r.json().get("values", [])]
    return json.dumps(pipes)

# ── Tool 4: Get Commit Diff ───────────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def get_commit_diff(repository: str, commit_hash: str) -> str:
    """Get changed files and line counts for a specific commit.
    Args:
        repository: Repository slug
        commit_hash: Full or short commit SHA
    """
    r = requests.get(
        f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{WORKSPACE}/{repository}/diffstat/{commit_hash}",
        headers=auth_headers(), timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    return json.dumps(r.json().get("values", []))

# ── Tool 5: Search Code ───────────────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def search_code(repository: str, query: str) -> str:
    """Search code in a Bitbucket repository.
    Args:
        repository: Repository slug
        query: Search query string (supports Bitbucket code search syntax)
    """
    r = requests.get(
        f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{WORKSPACE}/{repository}/search/code",
        headers=auth_headers(),
        params={"search_query": query}, timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    return json.dumps(r.json().get("values", []))

# ── Tool 6: Add PR Comment ────────────────────────────────────────
@mcp.tool()
def create_pr_comment(repository: str, pr_id: int, comment: str) -> str:
    """Add a review comment to a pull request.
    Args:
        repository: Repository slug
        pr_id: Pull request ID number
        comment: Comment text to post (supports markdown)
    """
    r = requests.post(
        f"{BBHOST}/repositories/{WORKSPACE}/{repository}/pullrequests/{pr_id}/comments",
        headers={**auth_headers(), "Content-Type": "application/json"},
        json={"content": {"raw": comment}}, timeout=30)
    r.raise_for_status()
    return json.dumps({"id": r.json().get("id"), "created": r.json().get("created_on")})

if __name__ == "__main__":
    mcp.run()

  


  

    
⚙️ Claude Desktop Config for Bitbucket MCP

    
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "bitbucket": {
      "command": "python",
      "args": ["/absolute/path/to/bitbucket_mcp.py"],
      "env": {
        // For Bitbucket Cloud:
        "BITBUCKET_HOST": "https://api.bitbucket.org/2.0",
        "BITBUCKET_TOKEN": "your-oauth2-or-app-password-token",
        "BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE": "your-workspace-slug",

        // For Bitbucket Server / Data Center (on-prem):
        // "BITBUCKET_HOST": "https://bitbucket.mycompany.com/rest/api/1.0",
        // "BITBUCKET_TOKEN": "your-personal-access-token",
        // "BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE": "your-project-key"
      }
    }
  }
}

  


  

    
🔬 Testing Your Bitbucket MCP Server

export BITBUCKET_WORKSPACE="your-workspace"

# 2. Run the MCP Inspector

#    Test list_repositories → should return your repos

#    Test get_pipeline_status → shows recent build results

  


  

    
🔧 The Same Pattern Works for Any Internal Tool

    

      

        
ToolTools to implementKey endpoints

        
          
Jirasearch_issues, create_ticket, update_status, add_comment/rest/api/3/issue, /rest/api/3/search

          
Jenkinslist_jobs, trigger_build, get_build_status, get_build_log/api/json, /job/{name}/build

          
Confluencesearch_pages, read_page, create_page/rest/api/content

          
PagerDutylist_incidents, acknowledge, add_note/incidents, /services

          
Your internal APIWhatever makes sense for your domainCheck your Swagger / OpenAPI spec

        
      

    

    

      💡 Pattern: If you have a REST API with Swagger docs, you can build an MCP server for it in under an hour. The FastMCP @mcp.tool() decorator is all you need. Each endpoint becomes one tool.

Build a custom MCP server that safely wraps kubectl (read-only commands only). Connect to Claude Desktop and debug Kubernetes issues in plain English.

    Tools to implement:
    
    
      
  • get_pods(namespace) — lists pods with status and restarts
    • 
      
  • describe_pod(name, namespace) — full pod description including events
    • 
      
  • get_logs(pod_name, tail=100) — recent log lines
    • 
      
  • get_events(namespace) — cluster events sorted by timestamp
    • 
      
  • get_resource_usage(namespace) — CPU/memory from kubectl top
    • 
    

    3-Step Roadmap:
    
    
      
  1. Build K8s MCP server — wrap subprocess calls to kubectl with read-only safety check
    2. 
      
  2. Configure Claude Desktop — test with "Why is my pod crashlooping?"
    3. 
      
  3. Add LangGraph for multi-step diagnosis — get pod → read logs → check events → diagnose
    4. 
    

    
Skills: FastMCP · subprocess · kubectl · LangGraph · Claude Desktop
